<p><i><b>The Dark Knight Rises</b></i> is a 2012 <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">superhero film</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>, who co-wrote the screenplay with his brother <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Nolan" title="Jonathan Nolan">Jonathan Nolan</a>, and the story with <a href="/wiki/David_S._Goyer" title="David S. Goyer">David S. Goyer</a>. Featuring the <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> character <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a>, the film is the final installment in <a href="/wiki/Batman_in_film#Christopher_Nolan" title="Batman in film">Nolan's <i>Batman</i> film trilogy</a>, and the sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i> (2005) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i> (2008). <a href="/wiki/Christian_Bale" title="Christian Bale">Christian Bale</a> reprises the lead role of Bruce Wayne/Batman, with a returning cast of allies: <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Oldman" title="Gary Oldman">Gary Oldman</a> as <a href="/wiki/James_Gordon_(comics)" title="James Gordon (comics)">James Gordon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Freeman" title="Morgan Freeman">Morgan Freeman</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Fox" title="Lucius Fox">Lucius Fox</a>. The film introduces <a href="/wiki/Catwoman" title="Catwoman">Selina Kyle</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a>), a sly, morally ambiguous cat burglar, and <a href="/wiki/Bane_(comics)" title="Bane (comics)">Bane</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenary</a> bent on destroying <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> who forces an older Bruce Wayne to come out of retirement and become Batman again.</p>
<p>Christopher Nolan was hesitant about returning to the series for a second time, but agreed after developing a story with his brother and Goyer that he felt would conclude the series on a satisfactory note. Nolan drew inspiration from Bane's comic book debut in the 1993 "<a href="/wiki/Batman:_Knightfall" title="Batman: Knightfall">Knightfall</a>" storyline, the 1986 series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="The Dark Knight Returns">The Dark Knight Returns</a></i>, and the 1999 storyline "<a href="/wiki/No_Man%27s_Land_(comics)" title="No Man's Land (comics)">No Man's Land</a>". Filming took place in locations including <a href="/wiki/Jodhpur" title="Jodhpur">Jodhpur</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> London, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>, Glasgow, Los Angeles, New York City, <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>. Nolan used <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> cameras for much of the filming, including the first six minutes of the film, to optimize the quality of the picture. A vehicle variation of the <a href="/wiki/Batplane" title="Batplane">Batplane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Batcopter" title="Batcopter">Batcopter</a> termed the "Bat", an underground prison set, and a new <a href="/wiki/Batcave" title="Batcave">Batcave</a> set were created specifically for the film. As with <i>The Dark Knight</i>, <a href="/wiki/Viral_marketing" title="Viral marketing">viral marketing</a> campaigns began early during production. When filming concluded, Warner Bros. refocused its campaign: developing promotional websites, releasing the first six minutes of the film, screening theatrical trailers, and sending out information regarding the film's plot.</p>
<p><i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> premiered in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> on July 16, 2012. The film was released in Australia and New Zealand on July 19, 2012, and in North America and the United Kingdom on July 20, 2012. Upon release it received critical acclaim and is widely considered by publications to be one of the best <a href="/wiki/2012_in_film" title="2012 in film">films of 2012</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Like its predecessor, the film grossed over $1 billion worldwide at the box office, making it the second film in the <i>Batman</i> film series, and by extension the second film based on a DC Comics character, to earn $1 billion. It is currently the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">eleventh-highest-grossing film of all time</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2012_in_film" title="2012 in film">third-highest-grossing film of 2012</a>, and the third-highest-grossing superhero film of all time.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span></h2>
<p>Eight years after <a href="/wiki/Two-Face" title="Two-Face">Harvey Dent</a>'s death, the Dent Act grants the <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City_Police_Department" title="Gotham City Police Department">Police Department</a> powers which nearly eradicate <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">organized crime</a>. Feeling guilty for covering up Dent's crimes, Police Commissioner <a href="/wiki/James_Gordon_(comics)" title="James Gordon (comics)">James Gordon</a> writes a resignation speech confessing the truth, but decides not to use it. <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a> has disappeared; Bruce Wayne has become a recluse. Cat burglar <a href="/wiki/Catwoman" title="Catwoman">Selina Kyle</a> obtains Bruce's fingerprints from his home, kidnaps a congressman, then disappears. Selina hands Bruce's fingerprints to Phillip Stryver, an assistant to Bruce's business rival John Daggett, in hope of having her criminal record erased. Stryver double-crosses Selina, but she uses the congressman's stolen phone to alert the police to their location. Gordon and the police arrive to find the congressman, then pursue Stryver's men into the sewers while Selina flees. A masked man called <a href="/wiki/Bane_(comics)" title="Bane (comics)">Bane</a> captures Gordon. Gordon escapes and is found by <a href="/wiki/Robin_in_other_media#The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="Robin in other media">John Blake</a>, a once-orphaned patrol officer who has deduced Batman's true identity from their similar backgrounds. Gordon promotes Blake to detective, with Blake reporting directly to him.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wayne_Enterprises" title="Wayne Enterprises">Wayne Enterprises</a> is unprofitable after Bruce discontinued his <a href="/wiki/Fusion_power" title="Fusion power">fusion reactor</a> project when he learned that the core could be weaponized. Later, Bane attacks the Gotham Stock Exchange, using Bruce's fingerprints in a transaction that bankrupts Wayne. <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a>, concerned that Bruce has not moved on from being Batman, reveals to him that <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Dawes" title="Rachel Dawes">Rachel Dawes</a> had intended to marry Dent before she died; Alfred then resigns in an attempt to dissuade Bruce. Fearing that Daggett, Bane's employer, would gain access to the reactor, Bruce asks Wayne Enterprises board member <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miranda_Tate" title="Miranda Tate">Miranda Tate</a> to take over his company. After being promised the software to erase her criminal record, Selina agrees to take Batman to Bane, but instead leads him into Bane's trap. Bane reveals that he intends to fulfill <a href="/wiki/Ra%27s_al_Ghul" title="Ra's al Ghul">Ra's al Ghul</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">mission to destroy Gotham</a> with the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Assassins" title="League of Assassins">League of Shadows</a> remnant. He engages Batman and delivers a crippling blow to his back, before taking him to a foreign, well-like prison where escape is virtually impossible. The inmates tell Bruce the story of Ra's al Ghul's child, born in the prison and cared for by a fellow prisoner before escaping—the only prisoner to have ever done so. Bruce assumes the child to be Bane.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, Bane lures Gotham police underground and collapses the exits. He kills Mayor Anthony Garcia and forces an abducted physicist, Dr. Leonid Pavel, to convert the reactor core into a nuclear bomb. Bane uses the bomb to hold the city hostage and isolate Gotham from the world. Using Gordon's stolen speech, Bane reveals the cover-up of Dent's crimes and releases the prisoners of <a href="/wiki/Blackgate_Penitentiary" title="Blackgate Penitentiary">Blackgate Penitentiary</a>, initiating a revolution. The wealthy and powerful have their property <a href="/wiki/Expropriation" title="Expropriation">expropriated</a>, are dragged from their homes, and given <a href="/wiki/Show_trial" title="Show trial">show trials</a> presided over by <a href="/wiki/Scarecrow_(DC_Comics)" title="Scarecrow (DC Comics)">Dr. Jonathan Crane</a>, where any sentence means likely death.</p>
<p>After months of recovery and re-training, Bruce escapes from the prison and enlists Selina, Blake, Tate, Gordon, and <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Fox" title="Lucius Fox">Lucius Fox</a> to help stop the bomb's detonation. While the police and Bane's forces clash, Batman defeats Bane, but Tate intervenes and stabs Batman, revealing herself to be <a href="/wiki/Talia_al_Ghul" title="Talia al Ghul">Talia al Ghul</a>, Ra's al Ghul's daughter. Talia escaped the prison aided by her fellow prisoner and protector, Bane. She plans to complete her father's work by detonating the bomb and destroying Gotham, but Gordon blocks her signal, preventing remote detonation. Talia leaves to find the bomb while Bane prepares to kill Batman, but Selina kills Bane using the <a href="/wiki/Batcycle#The_Dark_Knight_and_The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="Batcycle">Batpod</a>. Batman pursues Talia with the Bat, an aircraft developed by Fox, hoping to bring the bomb back to the reactor where it can be stabilized. Talia's truck crashes, but she remotely destroys the reactor before dying. With no way to stop the detonation, Batman uses the Bat to haul the bomb over the bay, where it detonates.</p>
<p>In the aftermath, Batman is presumed dead and is honored as a hero. With Bruce also presumed dead, Wayne Manor is left to the city to become an orphanage, and Wayne's remaining estate is left to Alfred. Fox discovers that Bruce had fixed the Bat's autopilot, and Gordon finds the <a href="/wiki/Bat-Signal" title="Bat-Signal">Bat-Signal</a> refurbished. While visiting <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, Alfred witnesses Bruce and Selina together. Blake resigns from the police force and inherits the <a href="/wiki/Batcave" title="Batcave">Batcave</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christian_Bale" title="Christian Bale">Christian Bale</a> as <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Bruce Wayne / Batman</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A billionaire socialite dedicated to protecting <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> from the criminal underworld. Nolan has stated that, due to the eight-year gap between the events of <i>The Dark Knight</i> and those of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, "he's an older Bruce Wayne; he's not in a great state."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EightYears_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-EightYears-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Bale employed a mixed-martial-arts discipline called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keysi_Fighting_Method" title="Keysi Fighting Method">Keysi Fighting Method</a>, but due to Bruce's current state and Bane's style, the method had to be modified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Bale has stated that <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> will be the final film in which he plays Batman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inquirer_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Inquirer-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> He describes the character's arc as finally confronting the pain of loss that he has deferred for years by fighting criminals balanced against the need to internalize that pain lest he give into his emotions and become the killer the city already believes him to be. Bale also acknowledged that Batman is not a flawless individual, that "he's not a healthy individual, this is somebody that is doing good, but he's right on the verge of doing bad. He's got that killer within him that he's desperately trying to not let off his leash. And that's what I always return to."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYDailyNewsWayne_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYDailyNewsWayne-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Bale clarifies that "He doesn't want to forget [his parents' deaths]. He wants to maintain that anger he felt at that injustice. But equally he wants to present this very vacuous, soulless persona to Gotham, so that hopefully no-one will suspect him but will just think he's a spoiled bastard."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NME_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NME-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Bale felt bittersweet about leaving the franchise, saying that it was like "saying goodbye to an old friend."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ColliderWayne_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-ColliderWayne-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Bruce's trusted butler and confidant. Alfred has acted as a father figure to Bruce, and continues to aid Bruce on his missions as well as supplying him with useful advice. Alfred is unable to accept Bruce's desire to revive his Batman persona, even going so far as to resign from his position to impress the seriousness of Bruce's position upon him. Christopher Nolan emphasized the emotional bond between Alfred and Bruce, stressing its importance in the previous films and predicting that the relationship will be strained as it never has before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gary_Oldman" title="Gary Oldman">Gary Oldman</a> as <a href="/wiki/James_Gordon_(comics)" title="James Gordon (comics)">James Gordon</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Commissioner of the <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City_Police_Department" title="Gotham City Police Department">Gotham City Police Department</a>, and one of the city's few honest police officers. Gary Oldman described the character's work in cleaning up Gotham City as having left him world-weary and slightly bored,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GordonCharacter_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-GordonCharacter-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> likening Gordon to a soldier who leaps at the chance to be on the front lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> His life has taken a turn for the worse since <i>The Dark Knight</i>; his wife has left him and taken their children, and the mayor is planning to dismiss him from his job. Gordon feels guilty over his role in covering up Harvey Dent's crimes to the point where he is prepared to resign from his position as Commissioner over it, but refrains from doing so when he senses that Gotham is about to come under threat.</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a> as <a href="/wiki/Catwoman" title="Catwoman">Selina Kyle</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jensen_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jensen-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastHathaway1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastHathaway1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Selina Kyle is a cat burglar, grifter, and <a href="/wiki/Femme_fatale" title="Femme fatale">femme fatale</a> who establishes a playful, teasing relationship with Bruce Wayne that "takes some of the somberness away from his character."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Kyle is pursuing a "clean slate", a computer program rumored to be able to erase a person's criminal history, when she crosses paths with both Bruce and Batman. Hathaway auditioned not knowing what role she was being considered for, admitting that she had one character in mind, but only learned that the role was Selina Kyle after talking with Christopher Nolan for an hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastHathaway3_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastHathaway3-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Hathaway described the role as being the most physically demanding she had ever played, and confessed that while she thought of herself as being fit she had to redouble her efforts in the gym to keep up with the demands of the role. Hathaway worked out five days a week for the role, including rigorous exercise and stunt training followed by an hour and a half of dance. She explained, "I've always thought that skinny was the goal, but with this job I also have to be strong."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harper.27sBazaar_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harper.27sBazaar-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Selena_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Selena-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Selena2_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Selena2-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Hathaway trained extensively in martial arts for the role, and looked to <a href="/wiki/Hedy_Lamarr" title="Hedy Lamarr">Hedy Lamarr</a>—who was the inspiration for the <a href="/wiki/Catwoman" title="Catwoman">Catwoman</a> character—in developing her performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher2_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher2-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a> as <a href="/wiki/Bane_(comics)" title="Bane (comics)">Bane</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jensen_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jensen-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A <a href="/wiki/Militant_(word)" title="Militant (word)">militant</a> <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">revolutionary</a> portraying himself as a "liberator", Bane is intent on destroying Gotham City. He was originally a member of the League of Shadows, before being <a href="/wiki/Excommunication" title="Excommunication">excommunicated</a>. The character was chosen by Christopher Nolan because of his desire to see Batman tested on both a physical and mental level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EightYears_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-EightYears-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banechoice2_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Banechoice2-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Costume_designer" title="Costume designer">costume designer</a> <a href="/wiki/Lindy_Hemming" title="Lindy Hemming">Lindy Hemming</a>, the character wears a mask that supplies him with an analgesic gas to relieve pain he suffers from an injury sustained "early in his story".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EightYears_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-EightYears-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Bane has been described as "a terrorist in both thought and action"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EightYears_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-EightYears-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> and is "florid in his speech, [with] the physicality of a gorilla".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Hardy intended to portray the character as "more menacing" than <a href="/wiki/Robert_Swenson" title="Robert Swenson">Robert Swenson</a>'s version of the character in <a href="/wiki/Joel_Schumacher" title="Joel Schumacher">Joel Schumacher</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_%26_Robin_(film)" title="Batman &amp; Robin (film)">Batman &amp; Robin</a></i> and that in order to do so, his portrayal entailed creating a contradiction between his voice and body. Hardy gained 30 pounds (14 kg) for the role,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filipponi_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filipponi-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> increasing his weight to 198 pounds (90 kg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filipponi_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Filipponi-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Hardy based Bane's voice on several influences, which include <a href="/wiki/Bartley_Gorman" title="Bartley Gorman">Bartley Gorman</a> as well as a desire to honor the character's intellect and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Prisca_(DC_Comics)" title="Santa Prisca (DC Comics)">Caribbean heritage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HardyVoice_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-HardyVoice-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Hardy describes Bane's fighting style as "Brutal. He's a big dude who's incredibly clinical, in the fact that he has a result-based and oriented fighting style. It's not about fighting. It's about carnage. The style is heavy-handed, heavy-footed, it's nasty. Anything from small-joint manipulation to crushing skulls, crushing rib cages, stamping on shins and knees and necks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EightYears_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-EightYears-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Bane proclaims that his revolution's enemies are the rich and the corrupt, who he contends are oppressing "the people", and fooling them with myths of opportunity. Political theorist and cultural critic <a href="/wiki/Slavoj_%C5%BDi%C5%BEek" title="Slavoj Žižek">Slavoj Žižek</a> likens Bane to a modern day <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a>, counter-intuitively driven to violence out of a sense of love, while others have called him a "high-tech <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maximilien_de_Robespierre" title="Maximilien de Robespierre">Robespierre</a> on steroids," a melded triad of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Lenin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">bin Laden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Steve_Austin" title="Stone Cold Steve Austin">Steve Austin</a> set on fomenting "<a href="/wiki/Proletariat" title="Proletariat">proletarian</a> retribution," and "the one thing that's worse than the second film's raving <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a>: a <a href="/wiki/Demagogue" title="Demagogue">demagogue</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marion_Cotillard" title="Marion Cotillard">Marion Cotillard</a> as <a href="/wiki/Talia_al_Ghul" title="Talia al Ghul">Miranda Tate / Talia al Ghul</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A member of the Wayne Enterprises executive board who encourages a still-grieving Bruce Wayne to rejoin with society and continue his father's philanthropic works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon-LevittandCotillard_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-LevittandCotillard-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Cotillard denied speculation that she would be playing a dual role as Miranda and Talia al Ghul, stating that her character is a completely original creation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastCotillard1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastCotillard1-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> though the final cut of the film revealed this to be misdirection. Tate was described as providing Bruce with a much-needed sense of hope at the behest of Alfred and Lucius Fox.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Child actress <a href="/wiki/Joey_King" title="Joey King">Joey King</a> portrays a young Talia in flashbacks.</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Gordon-Levitt" title="Joseph Gordon-Levitt">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a> as <a href="/wiki/Robin_in_other_media#The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="Robin in other media">John Blake</a>:</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>A young police officer whose instincts lead him to believe that there is trouble on the horizon. Seeing something of himself in Blake, Commissioner Gordon promotes him to detective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon-LevittandCotillard_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-LevittandCotillard-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Blake represents the idealism that Gordon and Bruce Wayne once held, but soon lost in their battle against crime in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-6"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The film reveals his legal name to be Robin John Blake, an homage to Batman's sidekick in the comics, <a href="/wiki/Robin_(comics)" title="Robin (comics)">Robin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Morgan_Freeman" title="Morgan Freeman">Morgan Freeman</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Fox" title="Lucius Fox">Lucius Fox</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>Fox runs <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Enterprises" title="Wayne Enterprises">Wayne Enterprises</a> on behalf of Bruce Wayne and serves as his <a href="/wiki/Armourer" title="Armourer">armorer</a>, providing him with high-tech equipment. His position as President of Wayne Enterprises allows him to discreetly develop cutting-edge technology and weaponry, even as Wayne Enterprises starts losing money.</dd>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cillian_Murphy" title="Cillian Murphy">Cillian Murphy</a> reprises his role as <a href="/wiki/Scarecrow_(DC_Comics)" title="Scarecrow (DC Comics)">Dr. Jonathan Crane / Scarecrow</a> from the previous films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Josh_Pence" title="Josh Pence">Josh Pence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a> both appear as <a href="/wiki/Ra%27s_al_Ghul" title="Ra's al Ghul">Ra's al Ghul</a>, leader of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/League_of_Shadows" title="League of Shadows">League of Shadows</a>; Pence plays a younger version of the character in scenes set thirty years before the events of <i>Batman Begins</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastPence_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastPence-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> while Neeson briefly appears to the imprisoned Bruce Wayne. Neeson stated that he was unaware of his role or if he would actually be in the movie, due to its secrecy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastNeeson_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastNeeson-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastNeeson2_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastNeeson2-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Other cast members include <a href="/wiki/Nestor_Carbonell" title="Nestor Carbonell">Nestor Carbonell</a> reprising his role as Mayor Anthony Garcia;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastGarcia_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastGarcia-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alon_Abutbul" title="Alon Abutbul">Alon Abutbul</a> as Dr. Leonid Pavel, a Russian nuclear physicist;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastAbutbul_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastAbutbul-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing2_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing2-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Juno_Temple" title="Juno Temple">Juno Temple</a> as Jen, friend and accomplice of Selina Kyle;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastTemple_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastTemple-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Modine" title="Matthew Modine">Matthew Modine</a> as Deputy Commissioner Peter Foley;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modine_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Modine-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ben_Mendelsohn" title="Ben Mendelsohn">Ben Mendelsohn</a> as Bruce Wayne's business rival John Daggett with <a href="/wiki/Burn_Gorman" title="Burn Gorman">Burn Gorman</a> playing his assistant Philip Stryver; <a href="/wiki/Brett_Cullen" title="Brett Cullen">Brett Cullen</a> as a congressman;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cullen_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cullen-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Ellis_(actor)" title="Chris Ellis (actor)">Chris Ellis</a> as a priest;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cullen_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cullen-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aidan_Gillen" title="Aidan Gillen">Aidan Gillen</a> as the CIA agent;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gillen_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gillen-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastGillen2_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastGillen2-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rob_Brown_(actor)" title="Rob Brown (actor)">Rob Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Harrington" title="Desmond Harrington">Desmond Harrington</a> as police officers;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastBrown_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastBrown-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Josh_Stewart" title="Josh Stewart">Josh Stewart</a> as Bane's right-hand man Barsad,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stewart_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Judge" title="Christopher Judge">Christopher Judge</a> as one of Bane's henchmen<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Judge_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Judge-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Conti" title="Tom Conti">Tom Conti</a> as a prisoner. <a href="/wiki/William_Devane" title="William Devane">William Devane</a> portrays the President of the United States. <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Eckhart" title="Aaron Eckhart">Aaron Eckhart</a> expressed enthusiasm in returning for a sequel if asked, although he later stated Nolan verified that his character, <a href="/wiki/Two-Face" title="Two-Face">Harvey Dent / Two-Face</a>, is dead,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CastEckhart_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-CastEckhart-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> and only archive footage of Eckhart from <i>The Dark Knight</i> appears in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Several members of the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> have cameo appearances as members of the fictional Gotham Rogues football team in the film, including <a href="/wiki/Ben_Roethlisberger" title="Ben Roethlisberger">Ben Roethlisberger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hines_Ward" title="Hines Ward">Hines Ward</a>, <a href="/wiki/Troy_Polamalu" title="Troy Polamalu">Troy Polamalu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Colon_(American_football)" title="Willie Colon (American football)">Willie Colon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maurkice_Pouncey" title="Maurkice Pouncey">Maurkice Pouncey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Wallace_(American_football)" title="Mike Wallace (American football)">Mike Wallace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heath_Miller" title="Heath Miller">Heath Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Smith_(American_football)" title="Aaron Smith (American football)">Aaron Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Clark_(American_football)" title="Ryan Clark (American football)">Ryan Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Farrior" title="James Farrior">James Farrior</a>, <a href="/wiki/LaMarr_Woodley" title="LaMarr Woodley">LaMarr Woodley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Casey_Hampton" title="Casey Hampton">Casey Hampton</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steelers-1_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steelers-1-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steelers-2_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steelers-2-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> and former Steelers head coach <a href="/wiki/Bill_Cowher" title="Bill Cowher">Bill Cowher</a> as the head coach of the Rogues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steelers-3_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steelers-3-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Pittsburgh mayor <a href="/wiki/Luke_Ravenstahl" title="Luke Ravenstahl">Luke Ravenstahl</a>, a kicker in college, appears as the kicker for the Rogues' opponents, the Rapid City Monuments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ravenstahl_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ravenstahl-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Rooney_family" title="Rooney family">Rooney family</a> sold a minority stake in the team to <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Tull" title="Thomas Tull">Thomas Tull</a>, the CEO and president of <a href="/wiki/Legendary_Pictures" title="Legendary Pictures">Legendary Pictures</a>, which produced <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steelers-4_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steelers-4-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Leahy" title="Patrick Leahy">Patrick Leahy</a>, who had made a cameo appearance in <i>The Dark Knight</i>, returned in <i>The Dark Knight Rises,</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-patrick_leahy_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-patrick_leahy-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> as a Wayne Enterprises board member. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lennon_(actor)" title="Thomas Lennon (actor)">Thomas Lennon</a>, who had appeared as a doctor in <i><a href="/wiki/Memento_(film)" title="Memento (film)">Memento</a></i>, once again plays a doctor. India Wadsworth plays the wife of Ra's al Ghul and the mother of Talia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:35%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"The key thing that makes the third film a great possibility for us is that we want to finish our story [...] rather than infinitely blowing up the balloon and expanding the story [...] Unlike the comics, these things don't go on forever in film and viewing it as a story with an end is useful. Viewing it as an ending, that sets you very much on the right track about the appropriate conclusion."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>, confirming his involvement in <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collidernofreeze_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-collidernofreeze-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Warner Bros. president of production Jeff Robinov had hoped a third film would be released in 2011 or 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development1_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development1-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan wanted the story for the third installment to keep him emotionally invested. "On a more superficial level, I have to ask the question," he reasoned, "how many good third movies in a franchise can people name?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development2_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development2-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan said that he never even thought a third film was possible in the foreword for his book <i>The Art and Making of the Dark Knight Trilogy</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan only agreed to a third film on the basis of finding a worthwhile story, fearing that he would become bored halfway through production if he discovered the film to be unnecessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development8_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development8-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> By December 2008, Nolan completed a rough story outline, before he committed himself to <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development3_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development3-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Later in December, <a href="/wiki/Alan_F._Horn" title="Alan F. Horn">Alan F. Horn</a> confirmed that while discussions with Nolan about a third film were ongoing, no casting had been done, and Horn denied all such rumors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development4_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development4-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Before Nolan confirmed his involvement, Gary Oldman had said he was confident Nolan would return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development5_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development5-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the success of <a href="/wiki/Joker_(comics)" title="Joker (comics)">the Joker</a> in <i>The Dark Knight</i>, studio executives wished for <a href="/wiki/Riddler" title="Riddler">The Riddler</a> to be included as the primary villain as he was considered a similar character and encouraged the casting of <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beginsending_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-beginsending-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Nolan wanted the antagonist to be vastly different from the previous incarnations and committed to using <a href="/wiki/Bane_(comics)" title="Bane (comics)">Bane</a> instead,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beginsending_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-beginsending-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> citing the need for a character with a physical presence within the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banechoice_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Banechoice-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> He was initially unfamiliar with the character's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Back-story" title="Back-story">back-story</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banechoice2_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Banechoice2-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> but pointed out the appeal of an archetype, labelling it as "the extreme of some type of villainy". When comparing the choice of Bane with the Joker, Nolan highlighted the Joker as an example of "diabolical, chaotic anarchy and has a devilish sense of humor", juxtaposing him against Bane, who he likened to "a classic movie monster [...] with a terrific brain."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banechoice_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-Banechoice-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It was not until February 9, 2010, that it was announced that Nolan had "cracked" the story of a sequel to <i>The Dark Knight</i> and was committed to return to the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development6_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development6-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Shortly afterward, it was announced <a href="/wiki/David_S._Goyer" title="David S. Goyer">David S. Goyer</a> and Jonathan Nolan were working on a screenplay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scriptunderway_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-scriptunderway-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Goyer would leave the project during pre-production to begin work on <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i>; Jonathan continued writing the script based on the story by his brother Chris and Goyer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Chris Nolan said that his brother's original draft was about 400 pages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's storyline has been compared with the <i>Batman</i> comic book series' story arc "<a href="/wiki/Batman:_Knightfall" title="Batman: Knightfall">Knightfall</a>" (1993), which showcased Bane; the mini-series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="The Dark Knight Returns">The Dark Knight Returns</a></i> (1986), in which Batman returns to <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> after a ten-year absence; and the story arc "<a href="/wiki/No_Man%27s_Land_(comics)" title="No Man's Land (comics)">No Man's Land</a>" (1999), which depicts a Gotham cut off from the rest of the world and overrun by gangs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ComicST_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-ComicST-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ComicClues_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-ComicClues-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The nickname "the Dark Knight" was first applied to Batman in <i>Batman</i> #1 (1940), in a story written by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Finger" title="Bill Finger">Bill Finger</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan confirmed the Joker would not return in the third film, and dismissed rumors that he considered using unused footage of <a href="/wiki/Heath_Ledger" title="Heath Ledger">Heath Ledger</a> from <i>The Dark Knight</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development9_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development9-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> reunited Nolan with many of his past collaborators, including cinematographer <a href="/wiki/Wally_Pfister" title="Wally Pfister">Wally Pfister</a>, production designer <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Crowley" title="Nathan Crowley">Nathan Crowley</a>, editor <a href="/wiki/Lee_Smith_(editor)" title="Lee Smith (editor)">Lee Smith</a>, costume designer Lindy Hemming, special effects supervisors Paul Franklin and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Corbould" title="Chris Corbould">Chris Corbould</a>, and composer <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development10_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Development10-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Batmobile_on_set.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2488" data-file-width="2488" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Batmobile_on_set.jpg/200px-Batmobile_on_set.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Batmobile_on_set.jpg/300px-Batmobile_on_set.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Batmobile_on_set.jpg/400px-Batmobile_on_set.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batmobile_on_set.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Batmobile" title="Batmobile">Tumbler</a> on the set of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During location scouting in December 2010, Nolan began searching for locations such as India, Romania, and Michigan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Location1_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Location1-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Location2_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Location2-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Location3_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Location3-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <i>Romania Insider</i>, Nolan was interested in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>'s historical centers, Edgar Quinet Street, the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Parliament" title="Palace of the Parliament">Palace of the Parliament</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Salina_Turda" title="Salina Turda">Turda salt mine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Location1_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Location1-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The film had an estimated budget of $250–300 million, coming down to about $230 million after tax credits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fritz_.26_Kaufman_.28July_17.2C_2012.29_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fritz_.26_Kaufman_.28July_17.2C_2012.29-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan elected not to film in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3-D_film" title="3-D film">3-D</a>, but instead stated that he intended to focus on improving image quality and scale using the <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> format.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming2_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming2-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> featured over an hour of footage shot in IMAX (by comparison, <i>The Dark Knight</i> contained 28 minutes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60Minutes_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-60Minutes-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ColliderIMAX_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-ColliderIMAX-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan had several meetings with IMAX Vice-President David Keighley to work on the logistics of projecting films in digital IMAX venues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ColliderIMAX_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-ColliderIMAX-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Wally Pfister had expressed interest in shooting the film entirely in IMAX,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming4_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming4-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> but because of the considerable noise made by IMAX cameras, <a href="/wiki/35_mm_film" title="35 mm film">35mm</a> and <a href="/wiki/70_mm_film" title="70 mm film">70mm</a> cameras had to be used for shooting the film's dialogue scenes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ColliderIMAX_82-2"><a href="#cite_note-ColliderIMAX-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40Minutes_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-40Minutes-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> as dialogue had to be dubbed when shot with IMAX cameras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ColliderIMAX2_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-ColliderIMAX2-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Chairman and president of the IMAX Corporation Greg Foster stated that IMAX plans to run the film in its theatres for two months, despite only being contractually committed to run the film for two weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2months_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-2months-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan also bypassed the use of a <a href="/wiki/Digital_intermediate" title="Digital intermediate">digital intermediate</a> for the film, resulting in less manipulation of the filmed image and higher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Film_resolution" title="Film resolution">film resolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DI_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-DI-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Filming was scheduled to start in May and conclude in November 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Semlyen_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Semlyen-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> commenced on May 6, 2011, in <a href="/wiki/Jodhpur" title="Jodhpur">Jodhpur</a>, India at the <a href="/wiki/Mehrangarh_Fort" title="Mehrangarh Fort">Mehrangarh Fort</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming5_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming5-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming6_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming6-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> before moving to <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, where it operated under the working title <i>Magnus Rex</i> to reduce the visibility of the production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming7_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming7-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CMU_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-CMU-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Shooting locations within the city included <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a>, the site of an <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming8_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming8-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> with members of the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> playing the Gotham Rogues football team. More than 11,000 extras were used to depict the shot sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-7"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steelers-1_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Steelers-1-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steelers-2_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Steelers-2-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Filming in Pittsburgh also took place at the <a href="/wiki/Mellon_Institute_of_Industrial_Research" title="Mellon Institute of Industrial Research">Mellon Institute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Software_Engineering_Institute" title="Software Engineering Institute">Software Engineering Institute</a> at <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CMU_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-CMU-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> A letter sent out to residents and business owners detailing road closures revealed that the streets of the city would be featured "as the start of [the] film".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming10_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming10-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/9-1-1" title="9-1-1">9-1-1</a> operators were told to expect an increase in calls related to gunshots and explosions in the film's production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schutte_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schutte-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The Pittsburgh leg of production wrapped after three weeks on August 21, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming13_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming13-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The next portion of the filming began in Los Angeles in late August and finished up on October 23 after nine weeks of filming. New York and New Jersey were the next places of filming. The <a href="/wiki/Trump_Tower_(New_York_City)" title="Trump Tower (New York City)">Trump Tower</a> replaced the <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Daley_Center" title="Richard J. Daley Center">Richard J. Daley Center</a> as the location for the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Enterprises" title="Wayne Enterprises">Wayne Enterprises</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TrumpTower_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-TrumpTower-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2011, shooting shifted to <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark, New Jersey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming11_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming11-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming12_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming12-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Newark_City_Hall" title="Newark City Hall">Newark City Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_Park_(Newark)" title="Military Park (Newark)">Military Park</a> were among the locations used for filming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming15_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming15-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Other shooting locations include London and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, the latter of which was used for "additional exterior filming".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming16_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming16-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Principal photography concluded on November 14, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming17_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming17-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The external waterfall scene at the end of the film was shot at <a href="/wiki/Sgwd_Henrhyd" title="Sgwd Henrhyd">Sgwd Henrhyd</a> falls, on the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Brecon_Beacons" title="Brecon Beacons">Brecon Beacons</a> National Park in <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>.</p>
<p>Production photos from filming in Pittsburgh showed a second <a href="/wiki/Batmobile#Batman_Begins.2C_The_Dark_Knight_and_The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="Batmobile">Tumbler</a> chassis after the first was destroyed, indicating that a new Batmobile would be in the film, following the destruction of the first in <i>The Dark Knight</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming18_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming18-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Further set photos revealed a "new vehicle" being transported to <a href="/wiki/Wabash_Tunnel" title="Wabash Tunnel">Wabash Tunnel</a>, prompting speculation as to its nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming19_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming19-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2011, Autoblog confirmed the presence of the new <a href="/wiki/Lamborghini_Aventador" title="Lamborghini Aventador">Lamborghini Aventador</a> on the film set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming20_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming20-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg/220px-Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg/330px-Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg/440px-Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wollaton_Park_MMB_07.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wollaton_Hall" title="Wollaton Hall">Wollaton Hall</a> in Nottingham was used as <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Manor" title="Wayne Manor">Wayne Manor</a>, Bruce Wayne's residence.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several accidents occurred during the production of the film. While filming at <a href="/wiki/Wollaton_Hall" title="Wollaton Hall">Wollaton Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Semi-trailer_truck" title="Semi-trailer truck">tractor-trailer</a> crashed into the main entrance, though no one was injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming21_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming21-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> A stuntman <a href="/wiki/Parachuting" title="Parachuting">parachutist</a> later crashed through the roof of a home in Cairngorm Gliding Club, Feshiebridge in Scotland, and became wedged there after a failed landing during a skydiving stunt; he was not seriously injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming22_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming22-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> While filming scenes in Pittsburgh, Hathaway's stunt double crashed into an IMAX camera while filming a sequence that required her to ride a <a href="/wiki/Batcycle#The_Dark_Knight_and_The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="Batcycle">Batpod</a> down a flight of stairs during a riot. There were no injuries, but the camera was destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BatpodCrash_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-BatpodCrash-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> A second accident took place in Pittsburgh when the truck carrying the then-unidentified vehicle later termed "the Bat" went off-course and crashed into a lighting array, damaging the model of the aircraft. Production was delayed while the model was repaired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming25_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming25-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly before Christmas of 2011, Christopher Nolan invited several prominent directors, including <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Wright" title="Edgar Wright">Edgar Wright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bay" title="Michael Bay">Michael Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Singer" title="Bryan Singer">Bryan Singer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eli_Roth" title="Eli Roth">Eli Roth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Jones" title="Duncan Jones">Duncan Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Daldry" title="Stephen Daldry">Stephen Daldry</a>, to Universal CityWalk's IMAX theatre for a private screening of the first six minutes of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, which had been shot on IMAX film and edited from the <a href="/wiki/Original_camera_negative" title="Original camera negative">original camera negative</a>. Nolan, feeling that the use of <a href="/wiki/Film_stock" title="Film stock">film stock</a> in cinema is currently being phased out due to the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinematography" title="Digital cinematography">digital cinematography</a> and projection, used this screening to make a case for the continued use of film, which he asserts still offers superior image quality to any digital format, and warned the filmmakers that unless they continued to assert their choice to use film in their productions, they may eventually lose it as an option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Traditionalist_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Traditionalist-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filmvsdigital_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-filmvsdigital-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan explained; "I wanted to give them a chance to see the potential, because I think IMAX is the best film format that was ever invented. It's the gold standard and what any other technology has to match up to, but none have, in my opinion. The message I wanted to put out there was that no one is taking anyone's digital cameras away. But if we want film to continue as an option, and someone is working on a big studio movie with the resources and the power to insist [on] film, they should say so. I felt as if I didn't say anything, and then we started to lose that option, it would be a shame. When I look at a digitally acquired and projected image, it looks inferior against an original negative anamorphic print or an IMAX one."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Traditionalist_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Traditionalist-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Costume_design">Costume design</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bane_Tom_Hardy5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="376" data-file-width="250" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e1/Bane_Tom_Hardy5.jpg/170px-Bane_Tom_Hardy5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e1/Bane_Tom_Hardy5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e1/Bane_Tom_Hardy5.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bane_Tom_Hardy5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A digitally mapped model of Tom Hardy's face and skull was used to design and construct Bane's mask.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Costume_designer" title="Costume designer">Costume designer</a> Lindy Hemming explained that Bane uses a mask to inhale an analgesic gas, which, in director Christopher Nolan's words, "keeps his pain just below the threshold so he can function." In designing Bane's costume, Hemming needed it to look "like an amalgam of all sorts of bits and pieces he cobbled together, as he passed through some very remote places. We made parts of his vest, for example, from fragments of an old military tent. His clothes are militaristic, but are not in any way a uniform." Hemming also designed Bane's mask to look "animalistic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-8"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design2_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Design2-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design5_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Design5-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Costume effects supervisor Graham Churchyard created a three-dimensional model of actor Tom Hardy's face and skull to design the mask, allowing the mask to perfectly conform to the contours of Hardy's face.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-9"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Hemming personally designed Bane's coat, which she admitted took two years to complete. Taking inspiration from a Swedish army jacket and a frock coat from the French Revolution, it was designed to make Bane look like equal parts dictatorial and revolutionary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-10"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The design was difficult as Hemming struggled to find a tailor in Los Angeles who could work with <a href="/wiki/Shearling" title="Shearling">shearling</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design4_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Design4-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Batsuit" title="Batsuit">Batsuit</a> consisted of 110 separate pieces, each of which had to be replicated dozens of times over the course of the production. The base layer was made of a <a href="/wiki/Polyester" title="Polyester">polyester</a> mesh that is utilized by the military and high-tech sports manufacturers because of its breathability and moisture-wicking properties. Molded pieces of flexible urethane were then attached to the mesh, to form the overall body armor plating. Carbon fiber panels were placed inside the sections on the legs, chest and abdomen. The cowl was sculpted from a cast of Bale's face and head to become a perfect fit for Christian Bale. The suit remained unchanged for the film since <i>The Dark Knight</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-11"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In creating Selina Kyle's catsuit, two layers of material were used, with the outer layer being <a href="/wiki/Polyurethane" title="Polyurethane">polyurethane</a> coated spandex, embossed with a hexagonal pattern. The catsuit also consisted of elbow-length gloves, a utility belt, and thigh-high boots with spike heels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-12"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_design">Production design</span></h4>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concept_artist" title="Concept artist">Concept artist</a> Tully Summers commented on Nolan's style of <a href="/wiki/Cinematography" title="Cinematography">cinematography</a> when asked about the difference between his designs for this film and fantasy-based designs for <i><a href="/wiki/Men_in_Black_3" title="Men in Black 3">Men in Black 3</a></i>: "The difference for me was Christopher Nolan's visual style. One of the things that makes his Batman movies so compelling is their tone of plausibility. He will often prefer a raw, grittier design over one that is very sleek and product design pretty. It's sort of a practical military aesthetic. This stuff is made to work, not impress shoppers. <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> is a war film."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Filming26_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Filming26-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Producer <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thomas" title="Emma Thomas">Emma Thomas</a> stated this Batman film has a different visual aesthetic from the first two Nolan-directed features, explaining that "it's meant to be winter in Gotham, so that right there is going to lend a whole different look to the film."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film introduces a vehicle that has been compared with the <a href="/wiki/Batplane" title="Batplane">Batplane</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Batcopter" title="Batcopter">Batcopter</a>, dubbed "the Bat". In designing the Bat, Nathan Crowley approached it as if it were an actual military project, emphasising the need for it to "fit into the same family" as the Tumbler and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batpod" title="Batpod">Batpod</a>. The final version of the Bat takes its design cues from the <a href="/wiki/Harrier_Jump_Jet" title="Harrier Jump Jet">Harrier Jump Jet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bell_Boeing_V-22_Osprey" title="Bell Boeing V-22 Osprey">Bell Boeing V-22 Osprey</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_AH-64_Apache" title="Boeing AH-64 Apache">Boeing AH-64 Apache</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-13"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Chris Corbould described the Bat's size and shape as presenting a major challenge for filming given Christopher Nolan's emphasis on practical effects over <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a>. In order to make the Bat "fly", it was variously supported by wires, suspended from cranes and helicopters, and mounted on a purpose-built vehicle with hydraulic controls to simulate movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-14"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design3_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Design3-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design6_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Design6-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When designing the Batcave set, Crowley and fellow production designer Kevin Kavanaugh hit upon the idea of flooding the Batcave and having Batman's equipment, the Batsuit and a supercomputer rise from the water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-15"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Another set was designed at Cardington as an "underground prison", a rough-hewn labyrinth of stone cells in a vast abyss with a 120 foot (37 m) vertical shaft leading to the surface. Exteriors above the prison were filmed in Jodhpur, India, chosen because the "forbidding landscape added to the desolation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-16"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises_(soundtrack)" title="The Dark Knight Rises (soundtrack)">The Dark Knight Rises (soundtrack)</a></div>
<p>In an interview in October 2010, composer <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a> confirmed that he would be returning to score <i>The Dark Knight Rises.</i> <a href="/wiki/James_Newton_Howard" title="James Newton Howard">James Newton Howard</a> was offered to return and write the score with Zimmer as he did for <i>Batman Begins</i> and <i>The Dark Knight</i>, but he chose not to because he noted that the chemistry established between Zimmer and Nolan during the making of <i>Inception</i> would make him seem like a "third wheel".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howard_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Howard-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Zimmer included several cues from the earlier scores, but explains that he wanted to go in a "completely different direction" for Bane's theme. While the theme accompanying Selina Kyle is deliberately ambiguous, the musical thread spanning throughout the trilogy was composed exclusively for Bruce Wayne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_11-17"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film features a prevalent <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Arabic" title="Moroccan Arabic">Moroccan</a> chant of the phrase <i>deshi basara</i> (proper transliteration: <i>teeji basra</i>) (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>: تيجي بسرعة), which translates to "rise up" (literally: "come quickly").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2011, Zimmer <a href="/wiki/Crowdsourcing" title="Crowdsourcing">crowdsourced</a> online audio recordings of the chant to be used in the film's score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Music1_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Music1-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKRChant_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKRChant-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> When asked about the chant for clarification, Zimmer said, "The chant became a very complicated thing because I wanted hundreds of thousands of voices, and it's not so easy to get hundreds of thousands of voices. So, we tweeted and we posted on the internet, for people who wanted to be part of it. It seemed like an interesting thing. We've created this world, over these last two movies, and somehow I think the audience and the fans have been part of this world. We do keep them in mind."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Music2_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Music2-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h2>
<p>The official website launched in May 2011 introducing a viral marketing campaign similar to the one used to promote <i>The Dark Knight</i>. The website streamed an encrypted audio file described by users as chanting. Users decrypted the audio to the Twitter hashtag, "#TheFireRises". Warner Bros. removed a pixel from the webpage for every tweet using the hashtag. The website revealed the first official image of Bane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing1_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing1-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="618" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/57/DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg/220px-DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/57/DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg/330px-DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/57/DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg/440px-DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DarkKnightRisesViral.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>TheDarkKnightRises.com</i> was replaced with a dossier of an "anonymous vigilante", presenting information on the suspect—as well as several accusations, and depicting a warning claiming that the "suspect should be considered armed and dangerous".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 2011, a teaser trailer leaked online before its official release with <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The studio released the teaser three days after the leak. The trailer received mixed responses; Stephen Spencer Davis of <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> wrote it successfully built hype,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> while Kofi Outlaw of ScreenRant showed disappointment, claiming it was more of an "announcement trailer" than an actual teaser trailer. Outlaw criticized the quality, writing that a scene depicting Commissioner Gordon in a hospital bed was overly dramatic, had "hammy" dialogue, and was difficult to understand due to Gordon's labored breathing. Outlaw wrote that the sweeping shot of Gotham City had poor CGI and was too reminiscent of the <i>Inception</i> trailer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Outlaw_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Outlaw-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The theatrical trailer leaked online, like the teaser trailer, before being released the following week attached to theatrical prints of <i><a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes:_A_Game_of_Shadows" title="Sherlock Holmes: A Game of Shadows">Sherlock Holmes: A Game of Shadows</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKRtrailer1_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKRtrailer1-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing3_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing3-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing4_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing4-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Critics noted political undertones with dialogue foreshadowing the theme of <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">income inequality</a> and an "<a href="/wiki/Occupy_movement" title="Occupy movement">Occupy Gotham</a>" campaign within the world of the story.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing5_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing5-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing6_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing6-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing8_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing8-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> Receiving more than 12.5 million views in the first 24 hours after its release, the trailer set the record for most combined downloads from <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>, beating the previous record held by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">The Avengers</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing9_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing9-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the second trailer for <i>The Avengers</i> again set the record with 13.7 million downloads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYDailyNews_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYDailyNews-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Warner Bros. attached a second theatrical trailer for <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> to theatrical prints of <i>The Avengers</i>. An "unnamed" Warner Brothers executive clarified that "We see this placement as a good strategic decision. We always want our trailers to be seen with films that people want to see—and a lot of people will be going to The Avengers!" The executive also commented that the trailer will "provide the best potential exposure for TDKR."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKRtrailer2_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKRtrailer2-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> Warner Bros. released the trailer online on April 30, 2012, approximately four days before they attached it to theatrical prints of <i>The Avengers</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKRtrailer3_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKRtrailer3-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Continuing a method used with <i>The Dark Knight</i> whereby the opening sequence of the film was attached to IMAX prints of <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Legend_(film)" title="I Am Legend (film)">I Am Legend</a></i> seven months before release,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKopening_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKopening-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> a six-minute prologue of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> was attached to 70mm IMAX prints of <i><a href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible_%E2%80%93_Ghost_Protocol" title="Mission: Impossible – Ghost Protocol">Mission: Impossible – Ghost Protocol</a></i>, again approximately seven months before release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6Minutes_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-6Minutes-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Critical reaction to the prologue was positive,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketingProlog1_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarketingProlog1-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketingProlog2_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarketingProlog2-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketingProlog3_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarketingProlog3-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> with one critic commenting that "no one gets to make a film on this kind of scale anymore. Except for Christopher Nolan," though a round-up of reviews highlighted the way many critics found Tom Hardy's dialogue very difficult to hear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketingProlog4_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarketingProlog4-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Addressing the issue in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, Nolan said "I think when people see the film, things will come into focus. Bane is very complex and very interesting and when people see the finished film people will be very entertained by him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BaneVoice_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-BaneVoice-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
