<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg/220px-Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg/330px-Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg/440px-Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batsignal_at_Highmark_building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bat-signal" title="Bat-signal">bat-signal</a> projected against the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Avenue_Place_(Pittsburgh)" title="Fifth Avenue Place (Pittsburgh)">Fifth Avenue Place</a> during filming in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Viral marketing campaigns for the film continued as magazine companies <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i> received "CIA documents" concerning a "Dr. Leonid Pavel", with its mugshot connected to actor Alon Abutbul. According to the first document, Pavel is a missing Russian <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physicist</a>, while the second document appears to be an edited transcript of a conversation discussing the handover of Dr. Pavel to the CIA by Georgian separatists, but with most of the conversation redacted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing2_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing2-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> These were later shown to be plot elements of the six-minute prologue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketingProlog1_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-MarketingProlog1-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> The official Twitter account later linked to another censored document, this time, referencing "Operation Early Bird". A website of the same name was discovered, revealing a countdown timer. When the countdown finished, the site presented a map showing all available theaters that would be screening the film's prologue earlier than its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earlybird_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Earlybird-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earlybird2_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Earlybird2-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> Various websites received a package that included a cylinder map of "strike zones", and a "fire rises" <a href="/wiki/T-shirt" title="T-shirt">T-shirt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing12_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing12-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 2012, the film's official website was updated with a "dossier" on a suspect named "John Doe" also known as "the Batman" for an arrest, with a list of several accusations. The premise of the campaign starts when the mayor of Gotham City "redoubles" the effort to capture Batman and anyone supporting his return in preparation for the upcoming "Harvey Dent Day". The site also includes an extensive list of real-world locations where "graffiti related to movement in support of the vigilante's return" is located. For each tweet of a specific location marked on the list, a frame of the second theatrical trailer for the film was released on a separate website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing21_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing21-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012, six months prior to the film's release, tickets for midnight IMAX showings in New York, San Francisco, and Los Angeles went on sale and sold out immediately. Purchased tickets surfaced for sale online for over $100, compared with their original price of $17.50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing10_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing10-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3064" data-file-width="4511" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg/220px-2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg/330px-2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg/440px-2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2012_British_GP_-_Lotus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Formula One team <a href="/wiki/Lotus_F1" title="Lotus F1">Lotus F1</a> carried a special livery to promote <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> at the <a href="/wiki/2012_British_Grand_Prix" title="2012 British Grand Prix">2012 British Grand Prix</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/American_International_Toy_Fair" title="American International Toy Fair">American International Toy Fair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mattel" title="Mattel">Mattel</a> unveiled figures for Batman, Bane, and Catwoman, and Batman's flying vehicle, the Bat. The Mattel figures will also be released in the "Movie Masters" line, featuring more highly detailed and articulated presentation, and Quiktek versions that feature interchangeable accessories. <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> is set to release building sets and mini-figures based on the film and incorporating other DC Comic characters. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Funko" title="Funko">Funko</a> is releasing a series of <a href="/wiki/Plush" title="Plush">plush</a> toys, <a href="/wiki/Mezco_Toyz" title="Mezco Toyz">Mezco Toyz</a> are releasing vinyl figures, and <a href="/wiki/Hornby_Railways" title="Hornby Railways">Hornby</a> are releasing the Batman Tumbler car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing11_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing11-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> Other partners include <a href="/wiki/Jakks_Pacific" title="Jakks Pacific">Jakks Pacific</a> who are creating novelty and large-scale figures and plush toys,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing13_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing13-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> and PPW Toys, who are creating a Batman themed <a href="/wiki/Mr._Potato_Head" title="Mr. Potato Head">Mr. Potato Head</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing14_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing14-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Various clothing items including shoes, t-shirts, hats and wallets are also being produced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing15_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing15-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A video game of the same name was released on the same day as the release of the film for the <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> devices for promoting the movie. The game features <a href="/wiki/Open_world" title="Open world">open world</a> with primary focus on stealth and combat. The combat system of the game is inspired from <a href="/wiki/Batman:_Arkham_Asylum" title="Batman: Arkham Asylum">Arkham Asylum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Batman:_Arkham_City" title="Batman: Arkham City">Arkham City</a>. It takes place in Gotham City, with a somewhat similar but still significantly different plot from that of the movie. <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> gave it a mediocre score of 5.5/10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film <a href="/wiki/Novelization" title="Novelization">novelization</a>, written by author <a href="/wiki/Greg_Cox_(writer)" title="Greg Cox (writer)">Greg Cox</a> and published by <a href="/wiki/Titan_Books" title="Titan Books">Titan Books</a>, was released alongside the film on July 24, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing20_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing20-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Warner Bros. partnered with <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Dew" title="Mountain Dew">Mountain Dew</a> to do a cross-promotion that included a special paint scheme on the number 88 <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Impala#NASCAR" title="Chevrolet Impala">Chevrolet Impala</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Motorsports" title="Hendrick Motorsports">Hendrick Motorsports</a> and driven by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr.</a> in the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing22_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing22-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> On June 17, 2012, the car won the <a href="/wiki/2012_Quicken_Loans_400" title="2012 Quicken Loans 400">2012 Quicken Loans 400</a> at <a href="/wiki/Michigan_International_Speedway" title="Michigan International Speedway">Michigan International Speedway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketing23_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketing23-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 4, 2012, the studio signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> team <a href="/wiki/Lotus_F1" title="Lotus F1">Lotus F1</a> to have the film's logos appear on the <a href="/wiki/Lotus_E20" title="Lotus E20">Lotus E20s</a> driven by <a href="/wiki/Kimi_R%C3%A4ikk%C3%B6nen" title="Kimi Räikkönen">Kimi Räikkönen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romain_Grosjean" title="Romain Grosjean">Romain Grosjean</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2012_British_Grand_Prix" title="2012 British Grand Prix">2012 British Grand Prix</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lotus_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lotus-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> Räikkönen and Grosjean went on to finish the race in fifth and sixth place respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Silverstone_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Silverstone-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> Warner Bros. had previously followed a similar promotion at the <a href="/wiki/2008_British_Grand_Prix" title="2008 British Grand Prix">2008 British Grand Prix</a>, when the now-defunct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_F1" title="Toyota F1">Toyota F1</a> carried a livery to promote <i>The Dark Knight</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toyota_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Two digital comic books entitled <i>Batman Origins</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i>The Dark Knight: Prologue</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> were released exclusively for <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Lumia_900" title="Nokia Lumia 900">Nokia Lumia</a> devices. A special movie application has also been released, featuring trailers, wallpapers, movie schedules and Batman trivias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> Limited editions of the <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Lumia_710" title="Nokia Lumia 710">Lumia 710</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Lumia_800" title="Nokia Lumia 800">Lumia 800</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Lumia_900" title="Nokia Lumia 900">Lumia 900</a> were also released featuring a laser-etched Batman logo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting_in_Aurora.2C_Colorado">Shooting in Aurora, Colorado</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2012_Aurora_shooting" title="2012 Aurora shooting">2012 Aurora shooting</a></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:35%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I would not presume to know anything about the victims of the shooting but that they were there last night to watch a movie. I believe movies are one of the great American art forms and the shared experience of watching a story unfold on screen is an important and joyful pastime. The movie theatre is my home, and the idea that someone would violate that innocent and hopeful place in such an unbearably savage way is devastating to me. Nothing any of us can say could ever adequately express our feelings for the innocent victims of this appalling crime, but our thoughts are with them and their families."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Director Christopher Nolan's reaction to the theater shooting in <a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Colorado" title="Aurora, Colorado">Aurora, Colorado</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nolan_shooting_reaction_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nolan_shooting_reaction-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>On July 20, 2012, during a midnight showing of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> at the Century 16 cinema in <a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Colorado" title="Aurora, Colorado">Aurora, Colorado</a>, a gunman wearing a <a href="/wiki/Gas_mask" title="Gas mask">gas mask</a> opened fire inside the theater,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hearld_Sun_shooting_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hearld_Sun_shooting-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> killing 12 people and injuring 70 others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fox_news_shooting_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_news_shooting-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shooting_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-shooting-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-complete_list_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-complete_list-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Police responding to the shooting apprehended a suspect later identified as 24-year-old <a href="/wiki/James_Eagan_Holmes" title="James Eagan Holmes">James Eagan Holmes</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shooter_name_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-shooter_name-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> shortly after arriving on the scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Australian_shooting_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Australian_shooting-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Initial reports stated that Holmes identified himself as "the <a href="/wiki/Joker_(comics)" title="Joker (comics)">Joker</a>" at the time of his arrest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holmes_Joker_1_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes_Joker_1-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holmes_Joker_2_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes_Joker_2-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> This claim was later retracted by police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> cancelled the Paris, Mexico, and Japan premieres of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paris_cancelled_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paris_cancelled-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mexico_and_Japan_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mexico_and_Japan-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> and suspended the film's marketing campaign in Finland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finland_cancelled_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Finland_cancelled-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> Several broadcast networks also suspended television ads for the film in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> The trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/Gangster_Squad" title="Gangster Squad">Gangster Squad</a></i>, another Warner Bros. movie included in the screening of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, was removed as it contains a scene which shows gangsters shooting submachine guns at moviegoers through the screen, similar to the shooting in Aurora.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Director Christopher Nolan released a public statement calling the shooting "unbearably savage".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nolan_shooting_reaction_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nolan_shooting_reaction-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> Other stars of the film released statements expressing their condolences, with star Christian Bale paying a personal visit to the survivors and the memorial in Aurora.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E.21_News_Dark_Knight_Rises_Shooting:_Christian_Bale_Visits_Victims_in_Hospital_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-E.21_News_Dark_Knight_Rises_Shooting:_Christian_Bale_Visits_Victims_in_Hospital-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span></h2>
<p>On July 6, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> held a special <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> screening of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> for more than one hundred reporters and critics. However, technical issues with the computer device synchronising the sound and picture forced the studio to postpone the screening by a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> The film later premiered on July 16 at the AMC Lincoln Square Theater in New York City, New York,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-world_premiere_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-world_premiere-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by a European premiere on July 18 at <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Square" title="Leicester Square">Leicester Square</a> in London, England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe_premiere_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europe_premiere-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was released in Australia and New Zealand on July 19,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ozrelease_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-ozrelease-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> and was later released in North America and the United Kingdom on July 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzkoff_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Itzkoff-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-releasedate_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-releasedate-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h3>
<p>Film review aggregator Rotten Tomatoes gave <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> a score of 88% based on 305 reviews and a rating average of 8/10. The site's consensus reads, "<i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> is an ambitious, thoughtful, and potent action film that concludes Christopher Nolan's franchise in spectacular fashion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, another review aggregator, assigned the film a weighted score of 78 out of 100, based on 45 critics, indicating "generally favorable reviews".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> reported that audiences gave the film an A grade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THE_Hollywood_REPORTER_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-THE_Hollywood_REPORTER-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i> granted the film a maximum score of five stars, stating that it is "a superhero film without a superhero," comparing it with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather_Part_II" title="The Godfather Part II">The Godfather Part II</a></i> and praising Hardy's performance as well as the film's intricate plot and narrative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> thought the film was "potent, persuasive and hypnotic" and that it was "more than an exceptional superhero movie, it is masterful filmmaking by any standard."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Playlists</i> Todd Gilchrist wrote "A cinematic, cultural and personal triumph, <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> is emotionally inspiring, aesthetically significant and critically important for America itself – as a mirror of both sober reflection and resilient hope."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> gave it a 9 out of 10, noting similarities in tone and theme to <i>Batman Begins</i> over the trilogy's second installment <i>The Dark Knight</i>, but also describing Bane as "that bit less interesting to watch" than Ledger's Joker, despite praising his "menacing voice" and "body language-driven performance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> scored the film four out of five stars, calling it a film of "granite, monolithic intensity", yet also calling it a "hammy, portentous affair".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_review_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_review-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> Andrew O'Hehir of <i><a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon</a></i> writes "if <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> is a fascist film, it's a great fascist film, and arguably the biggest, darkest, most thrilling and disturbing and utterly balls-out spectacle ever created for the screen".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evil_masterpiece_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-evil_masterpiece-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> gave the film three out of four stars, stating "the film begins slowly with a murky plot and too many new characters, but builds to a sensational climax."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ebert_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ebert-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> Film critic <a href="/wiki/Richard_Roeper" title="Richard Roeper">Richard Roeper</a> gave the film an "A", calling it "a majestic, gorgeous, brutal and richly satisfying epic", and citing the final scenes of the picture as "the best five minutes of any film this year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> The London Film Review gave the film a B and said "Nolan's film is a reminder that superheroes aren't merely a frivolous distraction, but an embodiment of our best selves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was crowned by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> as the best modern comic book superhero adaption on screen, outranking both its main summer blockbuster competitor, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">Marvel's The Avengers</a></i>, and the trilogy's previous installment <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014, <i>Empire</i> ranked <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> the 72nd greatest film ever made on their list of "The 301 Greatest Movies Of All Time" as voted by the magazine's readers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Daily_Mail" title="The Daily Mail">The Daily Mail</a></i> '​s Chris Tookey said that the film was bloated and overly long, and criticized the sombre tone and lack of humor, despite praising the film's visually-impressive set pieces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>'s Tom Charity said the film was a "disappointingly clunky and bombastic conclusion to a superior series" and called it Nolan's worst film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tom_Charity_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tom_Charity-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> Anthony Lane of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> says that the "story is dense, overlong, and studded with references that will make sense only to those intimate with Nolan's previous excursions into Batmanhood".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In reaction to fan backlash to some of the negative reviews, Rotten Tomatoes chose to disable user commentary for the film leading up to its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> Some fans had threatened violence against critics while others threatened to take down the websites of movie critics who had given the film a negative review.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commentary">Commentary</span></h4>
<p>Writing in <i><a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/David_Sirota" title="David Sirota">David Sirota</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Progressivism_in_the_United_States" title="Progressivism in the United States">progressive</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> political commentator compared <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> and the game <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty" title="Call of Duty">Call of Duty</a></i> to 1980s popular culture reflecting the political period of the time, accusing them of perpetuating a conservative agenda: "Just as so many 1980s pop culture products reflected the spirit of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reagan_Revolution" title="Reagan Revolution">Reagan Revolution</a>'s conservative backlash, we are now seeing two blockbuster, genre-shaping products not-so-subtly reflect the <a href="/wiki/Tea_Party_movement" title="Tea Party movement">Tea Party</a>'s rhetorical backlash to the powerful <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> zeitgeist."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hate_the_99_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hate_the_99-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> An article in <i>Variety</i> reported Chuck Dixon, the co-creator of the Bane character, as saying that Bane is "far more akin to an Occupy Wall Street type if you're looking to cast him politically."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> Catherine Shoard of the center-left<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> British publication <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> claimed the film "is a quite audaciously capitalist vision, radically conservative, radically vigilante, that advances a serious, stirring proposal that the wish-fulfilment of the wealthy is to be championed if they say they want to do good."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caped_capitalist_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caped_capitalist-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> In contrast, liberal commentator <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Chait" title="Jonathan Chait">Jonathan Chait</a> opined in <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> that "What passes for a right-wing movie these days is <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, which submits the rather modest premise that, irritating though the rich may be, actually killing them and taking all their stuff might be excessive."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> Writing in <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, Bryan Alexander called Bane "the ultimate occupier" and reported that Christian Bale was amazed that the script had "foreseen" the Occupy movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Nolan has denied the film criticizes the Occupy movement and insists that none of his Batman films are intended to be political: "I've had as many conversations with people who have seen the film the other way round. We throw a lot of things against the wall to see if it sticks. We put a lot of interesting questions in the air, but that's simply a backdrop for the story. What we're really trying to do is show the cracks of society, show the conflicts that somebody would try to wedge open. We're going to get wildly different interpretations of what the film is supporting and not supporting, but it's not doing any of those things. It's just telling a story. If you're saying, 'Have you made a film that's supposed to be criticizing the Occupy Wall Street movement?' – well, obviously, that's not true."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-It.27s_not_political_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-It.27s_not_political-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Alternatively, <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">politically-conservative</a> commentator <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">Rush Limbaugh</a> alleged that the film was biased against <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012 Republican presidential nominee</a> <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a> due to Bane's name being a <a href="/wiki/Homophone" title="Homophone">homophone</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bain_Capital" title="Bain Capital">Bain Capital</a>, the financial service company Romney used to head, despite the fact that the character has existed as a major Batman foe since 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EAOnline_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-EAOnline-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> In response, Nolan said that the comments were "bizarre",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> while Dixon and Freeman said that the comments were "ridiculous".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EAOnline_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-EAOnline-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly, comparisons between Bane and Bain have also been made by bloggers on both sides of the political spectrum,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EAOnline_217-2"><a href="#cite_note-EAOnline-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> with Democratic adviser <a href="/wiki/Chris_Lehane" title="Chris Lehane">Christopher Lehane</a> noting the similarities between the narratives of the film and the presidential campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EAOnline_217-3"><a href="#cite_note-EAOnline-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span></h4>
<p>Hours before the midnight release, several box office analysts suggested as much as a $198 million domestic opening weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Aurora_shooting#Shooting_in_Aurora.2C_Colorado" title="2012 Aurora shooting">mass shooting during a midnight screening of the film</a>, Warner Bros. decided to not report further box office figures for the movie until Monday, July 23, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jul_23_reporting_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jul_23_reporting-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, other distributors also delayed the release of their official estimates as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup> The shooting is also speculated to have hurt the ticket sales as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E!_Online" title="E! Online">E! Online</a> reported that a <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> audience member had stated that "this theater was kinda empty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> Some reports released on July 21, 2012 said that rival studios estimated that the film grossed $75 million to $77 million on its opening day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165_on-track_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-165_on-track-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75_Friday_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-75_Friday-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BO_report_Jul_21_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-BO_report_Jul_21-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> Warner Brothers shortly after released a statement to <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> stating that they delayed the release of their estimates for the opening day total of the film "out of respect for the victims and their families," and added "Warner Bros. Pictures will not be reporting box office numbers for <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> throughout the weekend. Box office numbers will be released on Monday."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Worldwide</dt>
</dl>
<p><i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> earned $448 million in North America, and $636 million in other countries, summing up to a worldwide total of $1 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mojo_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mojo-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Worldwide, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">tenth-highest-grossing film of all time</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-worlwide_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-worlwide-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> and the third-highest-grossing film of <a href="/wiki/2012_in_film" title="2012 in film">2012</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-world2012_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-world2012-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> It had a worldwide opening weekend of $248.9 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-worldopening_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-worldopening-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> The film set a worldwide IMAX opening-weekend record with $23.8 million (previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAXopening_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXopening-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> and also broke the record for the fastest movie to make over $50 million in IMAX theatres. IMAX CEO Richard L. Gelfond explained this by claiming, "Audiences are clearly seeking out and embracing the film the way it was meant to be seen – in IMAX."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50IMAX_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-50IMAX-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup> On the 2012 Labor Day weekend, it became the third film distributed by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> and the thirteenth film in cinematic history to cross the $1 billion mark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> The film also became the second movie (after <i>Avatar</i>) to reach $100 million in worldwide IMAX grosses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>North America</dt>
</dl>
<p><i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> opened on Friday, July 20, 2012. It earned an estimated $30.6 million in midnight showings, which is the second-highest midnight gross behind <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i> ($43.5 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30.6_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-30.6-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30_mil_midnight_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-30_mil_midnight-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup> It did, however, set an <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> midnight-gross record with $2.3 million (previously held by <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKR-IMAX_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKR-IMAX-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HP_shutter_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-HP_shutter-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> The film made $75.8 million during its opening day, which is the third-highest single and opening day tally of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 23, 2012, it was announced that the film grossed $160.9 million for its debut weekend, which was the third-highest opening weekend ever, at the time, behind <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">Marvel's The Avengers</a></i> ($207.4 million) and <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i> ($169.2 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall_Street_BO_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wall_Street_BO-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup> However, it did set an opening-weekend record for a <a href="/wiki/2D_computer_graphics" title="2D computer graphics">2D</a> film (previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)#Box_office" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_BO_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter_BO-265"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup> and an IMAX opening-weekend record with $19.0 million (previously held by <i>Marvel's The Avengers</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAX-TDKR_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMAX-TDKR-266"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup> The film also held the top spot at the box office for its second and third weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> In North America, it is the seventh-highest-grossing film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-domestic_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-domestic-269"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> the second-highest-grossing 2012 film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-domestic2012_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-domestic2012-270"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> and the third-highest-grossing superhero film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-superhero_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-superhero-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup> and film based on comics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-comics_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-comics-272"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Markets outside North America</dt>
</dl>
<p>Outside North America, the film opened with $88.0 million from 7,173 theaters in just 17 markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-openingover_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-THR-openingover-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> It was in first place at the box office outside North America for four consecutive weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-thirdover_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-thirdover-274"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR-fourth_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-THR-fourth-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> Its three largest markets are the UK, Ireland and Malta ($90.3 million), where it is the highest-grossing superhero film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TDKR-UK_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-TDKR-UK-276"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup> China ($52.8 million) and Australia ($44.2 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span></h3>
<p><i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> was released on November 28, 2012 in Hong Kong and New Zealand. On December 3, it was released in the United Kingdom, and on December 4, it was released in the United States. It is available on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a>, DVD, and as a <a href="/wiki/Digital_distribution" title="Digital distribution">Digital download</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-homemedia1_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-homemedia1-278"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> Coinciding with the release of this film, a box set of <i>The Dark Knight</i> trilogy was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxset_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxset-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
